# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# GCC DWARF Debug Info Generation Chain

## Your Task

Trace how GCC generates DWARF debug information in gcc. Find C++ source files implementing: the DWARF DIE (Debug Info Entry) creation, the debug info hook interface (called by the front end), the dwarf2out.cc output generation, and the line number table emission.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d, sg-evals/gcc--96dfb333.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/llvm-project--a8f3c97d` (llvm/llvm-project)
- `sg-evals/gcc--96dfb333` (gcc-mirror/gcc)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

Perfect! I've created a comprehensive answer documenting GCC's DWARF debug information generation chain. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Components Identified:

**1. Debug Info Hook Interface** (`gcc/debug.h`)
- `gcc_debug_hooks` structure defines the interface that the compiler front-end uses to report debug information
- Functions like `init()`, `finish()`, `early_finish()`, `early_global_decl()`, `late_global_decl()`, `function_decl()`, `type_decl()`, and `source_line()`

**2. DWARF DIE Creation** (`gcc/dwarf2out.h` and `gcc/dwarf2out.cc`)
- `die_struct` / `dw_die_ref`: The fundamental DIE structure
- `dw_attr_node`: DIE attributes
- `dw_val_node`: Attribute values
- Functions like `new_die()`, `gen_decl_die()`, `gen_subprogram_die()`, `gen_variable_die()`, `gen_type_die()`

**3. DWARF Output Generation** (`gcc/dwarf2out.cc`)
- `dwarf2out_init()`: Initialize output
- `dwarf2out_finish()`: Emit complete DWARF information
- `dwarf2out_early_finish()`: Early debug generation finish
- Assembly output of DIE information and abbreviation tables

**4. Line Number Table Emission**
- Handled through `source_line()` hook
- `dw_loc_list_struct` and `dw_loc_descr_node` track source locations
- Integration with final.cc for instruction scanning

**5. Assembly Output** (`gcc/dwarf2asm.cc`, `gcc/dwarf2asm.h`)
- Low-level assembly output of DWARF information

The answer.json file has been created at `/workspace/answer.json` with all relevant files, symbols, and a complete explanation of the DWARF generation chain.

See the\\n12:    GNU General Public License for more details.\\n13: \\n14:    You should have received a copy of the GNU General Public License\\n15:    along with this program; see the file COPYING3.  If not see\\n16:    <http://www.gnu.org/licenses/>.  */\\n17: \\n18: #ifndef GCC_DEBUG_H\\n19: #define GCC_DEBUG_H\\n20: \\n21: /* This structure contains hooks for the debug information output\\n22:    functions, accessed through the global instance debug_hooks set in\\n23:    toplev.cc according to command line options.  */\\n24: /* WARNING: Do not add new debug hook targets - DWARF will be the only\\n25:    way to speak debug to the middle-end once we are able to get rid of\\n26:    the remaining targets.  If you need alternate output formats instead\\n27:    generate them off the DWARF representation.  */\\n28: struct gcc_debug_hooks\\n29: {\\n30:   /* Initialize debug output.  MAIN_FILENAME is the name of the main\\n31:      input file.  */\\n32:   void (* init) (const char *main_filename);\\n33: \\n34:   /* Output debug symbols.  */\\n35:   void (* finish) (const char *main_filename);\\n36: \\n37:   /* Run cleanups necessary after early debug generation.  */\\n38:   void (* early_finish) (const char *main_filename);\\n39: \\n40:   /* Called from cgraph_optimize before starting to assemble\\n41:      functions/variables/toplevel asms.  */\\n42:   void (* assembly_start) (void);\\n43: \\n44:   /* Macro defined on line LINE with name and expansion TEXT.  */\\n45:   void (* define) (unsigned int line, const char *text);\\n46: \\n47:   /* MACRO undefined on line LINE.  */\\n48:   void (* undef) (unsigned int line, const char *macro);\\n49: \\n50:   /* Record the beginning of a new source file FILE from LINE number\\n51:      in the previous one.  */\\n52:   void (* start_source_file) (unsigned int line, const char *file);\\n53: \\n54:   /* Record the resumption of a source file.  LINE is the line number\\n55:      in the source file we are returning to.  */\\n56:   void (* end_source_file) (unsigned int line);\\n57: \\n58:   /* Record the beginning of block N, counting from 1 and not\\n59:      including the function-scope block, at LINE.  */\\n60:   void (* begin_block) (unsigned int line, unsigned int n, tree block);\\n61: \\n62:   /* Record the end of a block.  Arguments as for begin_block.  */\\n63:   void (* end_block) (unsigned int line, unsigned int n);\\n64: \\n65:   /* Returns nonzero if it is appropriate not to emit any debugging\\n66:      information for BLOCK, because it doesn't contain any\\n67:      instructions.  This may not be the case for blocks containing\\n68:      nested functions, since we may actually call such a function even\\n69:      though the BLOCK information is messed up.  Defaults to true.  */\\n70:   bool (* ignore_block) (const_tree);\\n71: \\n72:   /* Record a source file location at (FILE, LINE, COLUMN, DISCRIMINATOR).  */\\n73:   void (* source_line) (unsigned int line, unsigned int column,\\n74: \\t\\t\\tconst char *file, int discriminator, bool is_stmt);\\n75: \\n76:   /* Record a source file location for a DECL_IGNORED_P function.  */\\n77:   void (* set_ignored_loc) (unsigned int line, unsigned int column,\\n78: \\t\\t\\t    const char *file);\\n79: \\n80:   /* Called at start of prologue code.  LINE is the first line in the\\n81:      function.  */\\n82:   void (* begin_prologue) (unsigned int line, unsigned int column,\\n83: \\t\\t\\t   const char *file);\\n84: \\n85:   /* Called at end of prologue code.  LINE is the first line in the\\n86:      function.  */\\n87:   void (* end_prologue) (unsigned int line, const char *file);\\n88: \\n89:   /* Called at beginning of epilogue code.  */\\n90:   void (* begin_epilogue) (unsigned int line, const char *file);\\n91: \\n92:   /* Record end of epilogue code.  */\\n93:   void (* end_epilogue) (unsigned int line, const char *file);\\n94: \\n95:   /* Called at start of function DECL, before it is declared.  */\\n96:   void (* begin_function) (tree decl);\\n97: \\n98:   /* Record end of function.  LINE is highest line number in function.  */\\n99:   void (* end_function) (unsigned int line);\\n100: \\n101:   /* Register UNIT as the main translation unit.  Called from front-ends when\\n102:      they create their main translation unit.  */\\n103:   void (* register_main_translation_unit) (tree);\\n104: \\n105:   /* Debug information for a function DECL.  This might include the\\n106:      function name (a symbol), its parameters, and the block that\\n107:      makes up the function's body, and the local variables of the\\n108:      function.\\n109: \\n110:      This is only called for FUNCTION_DECLs.  It is part of the late\\n111:      debug pass and is called from rest_of_handle_final.\\n112: \\n113:      Location information is available at this point.\\n114: \\n115:      See the documentation for early_global_decl and late_global_decl\\n116:      for other entry points into the debugging back-ends for DECLs.  */\\n117:   void (* function_decl) (tree decl);\\n118: \\n119:   /* Debug information for a global DECL.  Called from the parser\\n120:      after the parsing process has finished.\\n121: \\n122:      This gets called for both variables and functions.\\n123: \\n124:      Location information is not available at this point, but it is a\\n125:      good probe point to get access to symbols before they get\\n126:      optimized away.\\n127: \\n128:      This hook may be called on VAR_DECLs or FUNCTION_DECLs.  It is up\\n129:      to the hook to use what it needs.  */\\n130:   void (* early_global_decl) (tree decl);\\n131: \\n132:   /* Augment debug information generated by early_global_decl with\\n133:      more complete debug info (if applicable).  Called from toplev.cc\\n134:      after the compilation proper has finished and cgraph information\\n135:      is available.\\n136: \\n137:      This gets called for both variables and functions.\\n138: \\n139:      Location information is usually available at this point, unless\\n140:      the hook is being called for a decl that has been optimized away.\\n141: \\n142:      This hook may be called on VAR_DECLs or FUNCTION_DECLs.  It is up\\n143:      to the hook to use what it needs.  */\\n144:   void (* late_global_decl) (tree decl);\\n145: \\n146:   /* Debug information for a type DECL. debug info hook interface is defined in gcc/debug.h as the `gcc_debug_hooks` structure. This structure contains function pointers that the compiler front-end calls during compilation. The key hooks include:\\n- `init()`: Initialize debug output\\n- `finish()`: Output final debug symbols\\n- `early_finish()`: Run cleanups after early debug generation\\n- `assembly_start()`: Called from cgraph_optimize before assembling functions/variables\\n- `early_global_decl()`: Called for global declarations during parsing\\n- `late_global_decl()`: Called after compilation for variables and functions\\n- `function_decl()`: Debug information for function declarations\\n- `type_decl()`: Debug information for type declarations\\n- `source_line()`: Record source file location\\n- `begin_prologue()`, `end_prologue()`: Prologue code markers\\n\\n## DWARF DIE (Debug Info Entry) Creation\\nThe DIE structures are defined in gcc/dwarf2out.h:\\n- `die_struct`: The main DIE structure (typedef'd as `dw_die_ref`)\\n- `dw_attr_node`: Represents DIE attributes (combination of attribute kind and value)\\n- `dw_val_node`: Represents attribute values with support for various types (addresses, offsets, location lists, constants, strings, references, etc.)\\n- `dw_loc_descr_node`: Represents location descriptions (sequences of stack machine operations)\\n\\nThe gcc/dwarf2out.cc file implements DIE creation functions:\\n- `new_die()`: Creates new DIE entries\\n- `gen_decl_die()`: Generates DIEs for declarations\\n- `gen_subprogram_die()`: Generates DIEs for subprograms/functions\\n- `gen_variable_die()`: Generates DIEs for variables\\n- `gen_type_die()`: Generates DIEs for types\\n- `gen_typedef_die()`: Generates DIEs for typedefs\\n- `gen_struct_or_union_type_die()`: Generates DIEs for struct/union types\\n\\n## DWARF Output Generation\\nThe main output generation file is gcc/dwarf2out.cc, which contains:\\n- `dwarf2out_init()`: Initializes DWARF debug output at the start of compilation\\n- `dwarf2out_early_finish()`: Finish early debug generation\\n- `dwarf2out_finish()`: Main function to emit complete DWARF information at end of compilation\\n- Functions to output DIE information and build abbreviation tables\\n\\n## Line Number Table Emission\\nLine number information is handled through:\\n- The `source_line()` hook in gcc_debug_hooks (called from final.cc during instruction scanning)\\n- Location tracking in dw_loc_list_struct and dw_loc_descr_node\\n- Variables and location lists maintain source file, line, and column information\\n- Final assembly output of line number information in DWARF sections\\n\\n## Assembly Output\\nThe gcc/dwarf2asm.cc and gcc/dwarf2asm.h files handle the low-level assembly output of DWARF information.\\n\\n## Call Frame Information (CFI)\\nThe gcc/dwarf2cfi.cc file implements DWARF call frame information, generating CFI instructions through the `dwarf2out_emit_cfi()` function.\\n\\n## Integration Point\\nIn gcc/toplev.cc, the compiler initializes `debug_hooks` to point to `dwarf2_debug_hooks` (the instance of gcc_debug_hooks structure initialized in dwarf2out.cc) based on compilation flags (dwarf_debuginfo_p(), ctf_debuginfo_p(), btf_debuginfo_p(), etc.).\\n\\nThe entire pipeline flows from front-end declarations being reported via debug hooks \u2192 DIE creation in dwarf2out.cc \u2192 attribute and value assignment \u2192 final assembly output through dwarf2asm.cc.\"\n}\n",
